Then the duo received their own animated show, <i><a href="/wiki/Timon_%26_Pumbaa_(TV_series)" title="Timon &amp; Pumbaa (TV series)">The Lion King's Timon and Pumbaa</a></i>, which ran for three seasons and 85 episodes between 1995 and 1999. Ernie Sabella continued to voice Pumbaa, while Timon was voiced by <a href="/wiki/Quinton_Flynn" title="Quinton Flynn">Quinton Flynn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Schon" title="Kevin Schon">Kevin Schon</a> in addition to Nathan Lane himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Disney released two direct-to-video films related to <i>The Lion King</i>. The first was sequel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King_II:_Simba%27s_Pride" title="The Lion King II: Simba's Pride">The Lion King II: Simba's Pride</a></i>, issued in 1998 on VHS. The film centers around Simba and Nala's daughter, Kiara, who falls in love with Kovu, a male lion who was raised in a pride of Scar's followers, the Outsiders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> 2004 saw the release of another <i>Lion King</i> film on DVD, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King_1%C2%BD" title="The Lion King 1½">The Lion King 1½</a></i>. It is a prequel in showing how Timon and Pumbaa met each other, and also a <a href="/wiki/Sequel#Parallel" title="Sequel">parallel</a> in that it also depicts what the characters were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Retconned" title="Retconned">retconned</a> to have done during the events of the original movie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2014, it was announced that a new TV series based on the film will be released called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_Guard_(TV_series)" title="The Lion Guard (TV series)">The Lion Guard</a></i> and it will feature Kion, the son of Simba. It will be broadcast on <a href="/wiki/Disney_Junior" title="Disney Junior">Disney Junior</a> first as a television film on November 2015 before episodes broadcast in January 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King_(video_game)" title="The Lion King (video game)">The Lion King (video game)</a></div>
<p>Along with the film release, three different video games based on <i>The Lion King</i> were released by <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Interactive" title="Virgin Interactive">Virgin Interactive</a> on December 1994. The main title was developed by <a href="/wiki/Westwood_Studios" title="Westwood Studios">Westwood Studios</a>, and published for <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">PC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amiga" title="Amiga">Amiga</a> computers and the consoles <a href="/wiki/Super_Nintendo_Entertainment_System" title="Super Nintendo Entertainment System">SNES</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sega_Mega_Drive" title="Sega Mega Drive">Sega Mega Drive/Genesis</a>. Dark Technologies created the <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy" title="Game Boy">Game Boy</a> version, while Syrox Developments handled the <a href="/wiki/Master_System" title="Master System">Master System</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Game_Gear" title="Game Gear">Game Gear</a> version.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> The film and sequel <i>Simba's Pride</i> later inspired another game, <a href="/wiki/Torus_Games" title="Torus Games">Torus Games</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King:_Simba%27s_Mighty_Adventure" title="The Lion King: Simba's Mighty Adventure">The Lion King: Simba's Mighty Adventure</a></i> (2000) for the <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy_Color" title="Game Boy Color">Game Boy Color</a> and <a href="/wiki/PlayStation" title="PlayStation">PlayStation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> Timon and Pumbaa also appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/Timon_%26_Pumbaa%27s_Jungle_Games" title="Timon &amp; Pumbaa's Jungle Games">Timon &amp; Pumbaa's Jungle Games</a></i>, a 1995 PC game collection of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puzzle_game" title="Puzzle game">puzzle games</a> by <a href="/wiki/7th_Level" title="7th Level">7th Level</a>, later ported to the SNES by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiertex" title="Tiertex">Tiertex</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Square_Enix" title="Square Enix">Square Enix</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_Hearts" title="Kingdom Hearts">Kingdom Hearts</a></i> features Simba as a recurring <a href="/wiki/Gameplay_of_Final_Fantasy#Magic" title="Gameplay of Final Fantasy">summon</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KH-StrategyGuide_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-KH-StrategyGuide-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as a playable in the <i>Lion King</i> world, known as Pride Lands, in <i><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_Hearts_II" title="Kingdom Hearts II">Kingdom Hearts II</a></i>. There the plotline is loosely related to the later part of the original film, with all of the main characters except Zazu and Sarabi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Lion King</i> also provides one of the worlds featured in the 2011 action-adventure game <i><a href="/wiki/Disney_Universe" title="Disney Universe">Disney Universe</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> and Simba was featured in the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">Nintendo DS</a> title <i><a href="/wiki/Disney_Friends" title="Disney Friends">Disney Friends</a></i> (2008).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stage_adaptations">Stage adaptations</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King_(musical)" title="The Lion King (musical)">The Lion King (musical)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Il_Re_Leone_Insegne_in_Time_Square.jpg"><img alt="The façade of Minskoff Theatre at Broadway, with banners promoting the Lion King musical." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="642" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Il_Re_Leone_Insegne_in_Time_Square.jpg/150px-Il_Re_Leone_Insegne_in_Time_Square.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Il_Re_Leone_Insegne_in_Time_Square.jpg/225px-Il_Re_Leone_Insegne_in_Time_Square.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Il_Re_Leone_Insegne_in_Time_Square.jpg/300px-Il_Re_Leone_Insegne_in_Time_Square.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Il_Re_Leone_Insegne_in_Time_Square.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Advertisements for the musical adaptation of <i>The Lion King</i> at <a href="/wiki/Minskoff_Theatre" title="Minskoff Theatre">Minskoff Theatre</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Disney_Theatrical_Productions" title="Disney Theatrical Productions">Walt Disney Theatrical</a> produced a musical stage adaptation of the same name, which premiered in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minneapolis,_Minnesota" title="Minneapolis, Minnesota">Minneapolis, Minnesota</a> in July 1997, and later opened on <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway</a> in October 1997 at the <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam_Theatre" title="New Amsterdam Theatre">New Amsterdam Theatre</a>. <a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King_(musical)" title="The Lion King (musical)"><i>The Lion King</i> musical</a> was directed by <a href="/wiki/Julie_Taymor" title="Julie Taymor">Julie Taymor</a> and featured songs from both the movie and <i>Rhythm of the Pride Lands</i>, along with three new compositions by Elton John and Tim Rice. Mark Mancina did the musical arrangements and new orchestral tracks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> The musical became one of the most successful in Broadway history, winning six <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tony_Awards" title="Tony Awards">Tony Awards</a> including <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Musical">Best Musical</a>, and despite moving to the <a href="/wiki/Minskoff_Theatre" title="Minskoff Theatre">Minskoff Theatre</a> in 2006, is still running to this day in New York, becoming the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_longest-running_Broadway_shows" title="List of the longest-running Broadway shows">fourth longest-running show</a> and highest grossing Broadway production in history. The show's financial success led to adaptations all over the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schu_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-schu-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>The Lion King</i> inspired two attractions retelling the story of the film at <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Parks_and_Resorts" title="Walt Disney Parks and Resorts">Walt Disney Parks and Resorts</a>. The first, "<a href="/wiki/The_Legend_of_the_Lion_King" title="The Legend of the Lion King">The Legend of the Lion King</a>", featured a recreation of the film through life size puppets of its characters, and ran from 1994 to 2002 at <a href="/wiki/Magic_Kingdom" title="Magic Kingdom">Magic Kingdom</a> in <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_World" title="Walt Disney World">Walt Disney World</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> Another that is still running is the live-action 30-minute musical revue of the movie, "<a href="/wiki/Festival_of_the_Lion_King" title="Festival of the Lion King">Festival of the Lion King</a>", which incorporates the musical numbers into gymnastic routines with live actors, along with animatronic puppets of Simba and Pumba and a costumed actor as Timon. The attraction opened in April 1998 at Disney World's <a href="/wiki/Disney%27s_Animal_Kingdom" title="Disney's Animal Kingdom">Animal Kingdom</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> and in September 2005 in <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Disneyland" title="Hong Kong Disneyland">Hong Kong Disneyland</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Adventureland_(Disney)" title="Adventureland (Disney)">Adventureland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> A similar version under the name "The Legend of the Lion King" was featured in <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Paris" title="Disneyland Paris">Disneyland Paris</a> from 2004 to 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup><br style="clear:both;"/></p>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row">Live-action films<br/>
with animation</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-even" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row" style="padding-left:0;padding-right:0;">
